## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of position x) and possibly damping forces (functions of velocity v). Classical nonlinear oscillators include Duffing, Van der Pol, and other variants with polynomial or transcendental nonlinearities in x and v.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring force with linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring force with linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order polynomial restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic velocity-dependent damping)
- Forced oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonic external driving force)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (nonlinear restoring and damping)
- Pendulum-like oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force approximating pendulum)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (multiplicative coupling between position and velocity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells typical of Duffing-type oscillators
- Velocity-dependent terms linear in v → linear viscous damping or energy injection
- Products of x**2 and v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type self-excitation
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) → pendulum-like or periodic potential dynamics
- Odd symmetry in restoring force f(-x) = -f(x) → conservative symmetric potential about equilibrium
- Cubic velocity terms v**3 → nonlinear drag or Rayleigh-type dissipation
- Time-dependent sinusoidal terms sin(c*t) → external periodic forcing / parametric excitation
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system where phase portrait fully characterizes dynamics

I need to determine which candidates can match the ground truth:

**GT:** `-0.493165631499977*v*(1 - x**2) - 1.16769962902767*x*exp(-Abs(x))`

Expanding: `0.493165631499977*v*x**2 - 0.493165631499977*v - 1.16769962902767*x*exp(-Abs(x))`

The key components are:
1. A term proportional to `v*x²`
2. A term proportional to `v`
3. A term proportional to `x*exp(-|x|)`

The critical challenge is matching `x*exp(-|x|)`. Note that `exp(-|x|)` is NOT the same as `exp(-x)` or `exp(x)` since x takes both signs.

Let me analyze candidates systematically. I'll focus on whether each candidate can produce the `x*exp(-|x|)` term (or equivalent).

**Key observations about `x*exp(-|x|)`:**
- This is an odd function of x
- For x > 0: `x*exp(-x)`, for x < 0: `x*exp(x)`
- It cannot be represented by polynomials, `sin`, `exp(ax²)·sin(bx)`, `exp(ax)`, `log(exp(cx)+1)`, or polynomial combinations thereof

Let me check each candidate type:

**Polynomial-only candidates** (1, 71, 72, 88, 89, etc.): Cannot match `x*exp(-|x|)`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates with `sin` terms**: `sin` cannot reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates with `exp(c*x²)*sin(c*x)`**: Let me check - for x>0, `x*exp(-x)` vs `exp(cx²)*sin(dx)`. These are fundamentally different function classes. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates with `exp(c*x)`**: `exp(cx)` only works for one sign of x. Since `exp(-|x|)` behaves differently for positive and negative x, a single `exp(cx)` cannot match. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates with `log(c*exp(cx)+1)`**: This is a softplus-like function, cannot match `x*exp(-|x|)`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates with `t` dependence**: GT has no `t` dependence. Setting `t` coefficients to 0 reduces these to simpler forms - need to check what remains.

**Candidates with `x**c` (power terms)**: `x**c` for non-integer c has domain issues for negative x. Cannot match `x*exp(-|x|)`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates with `exp(c*sin(...))`**: Cannot match `x*exp(-|x|)`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates with `v*x**c`** (Candidate 58, 62): These have domain issues for negative x and wrong functional form. [NO MATCH]

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain a term that can produce `x*exp(-|x|)` or its equivalent. The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is a very specific non-analytic function (due to `|x|`) that cannot be represented by any combination of:
- Polynomials
- `exp(ax)`, `exp(ax²)`
- `sin`, `cos`
- `log(exp(cx)+1)`
- Power functions `x^c`

Every candidate falls into one of these categories. None can match the GT.

Let me verify candidates with `exp(c*x²)*sin(c*x)` more carefully (e.g., Candidate 5): `exp(cx²)*sin(dx)` - for large |x|, this grows exponentially (if c>0) or decays super-exponentially (if c<0), neither matching `x*exp(-|x|)`.
